    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/167921-did-you-guys-know-that-they-are-making-an">Did you guys know that they are making an anime series for this book?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_167921'><a id="like_count_community_question_167921" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/167921?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">12 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F19314.Ronia_the_Robber_s_Daughter">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5631155-elysse-breaux"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1308083548i/5631155._UX100_CR0,2,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5631155-elysse-breaux">Elysse Breaux</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The CG anime, "Sanzoku no Musume Rōnya", is done by Studio Ghibli, produced by Goro Miyazaki, son of Hayao Miyazki, and currently airing as a 26 episo<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The CG anime, "Sanzoku no Musume Rōnya", is done by Studio Ghibli, produced by Goro Miyazaki, son of Hayao Miyazki, and currently airing as a 26 episode series (as of today's date 3 episodes are released). It's under the title "Sanzoku no Musume Rōnya" for anyone who wants to check it out, just Google it! <br /><br />Hopefully it will be dubbed in English/Swedish in the future but in the meantime there are English subtitles! <br /><br />So far it's spot on with the book (character's looks, the dialogue and events) though it will probably expand Ronia's adventures in the forest. Definitely worth checking it out, especially if you're a Studio Ghibli fan.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_977312354" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/977312354" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480492067p2/32532774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/977312354?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789129548778" href="/book/show/469066.Ronja_r_vardotter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=astrid-lindgren">astrid-lindgren</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=children">children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer977312354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11945726119238529670">The tragedy of Romeo and Juliet with a happy ending! <br/><br/>Two clans of robbers, enemies for as long as the two chiefs Mattis and Borka can remember, share a forest and a castle split in two by a giant lightning, and a common enemy in the knights of the crown. Bad-mannered, ill-tempered, violent and boastful, they live their robber's lives between the magical and dangerous creatures of the woods...<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491581027i/22425287._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>... until one day, they meet a challenge where they least expect it: in their own children!<br/><br/>Ronja, Mattis'</span>
  <span id="freeText11945726119238529670" style="display:none">The tragedy of Romeo and Juliet with a happy ending! <br><br>Two clans of robbers, enemies for as long as the two chiefs Mattis and Borka can remember, share a forest and a castle split in two by a giant lightning, and a common enemy in the knights of the crown. Bad-mannered, ill-tempered, violent and boastful, they live their robber's lives between the magical and dangerous creatures of the woods...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491581027i/22425287._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>... until one day, they meet a challenge where they least expect it: in their own children!<br><br>Ronja, Mattis' daughter, and Birk Borkasson are true children of Sweden's natural spirit. Wild, confident, at home in the forest, and with a mind of their own, not bowing to parents or traditions. Becoming friends, they defy their fathers and move out of the divided castle to build a future for themselves beyond the dogmatic hate of their clans. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491581027i/22425286._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In a cave in the forest, they learn skills for life, and how to face dangers bravely, and conflicts not so bravely, but passionately enough.<br><br>Omnipresent is the threat of Swedish winter: the two children know they won't survive the harsh climate, and the short summer all too quickly turns into cold and rainy autumn. Stubbornly, they refuse to return to their families until peace is made, and until they are allowed to be friends.<br><br>In the end, Mattis reaches out to save his daughter's life, and the two clans are united under one chief. In typical robber's code, the physically strongest of the chiefs will become leader, and Mattis wins the fight. At the celebrations in the castle afterwards, Mattis and Borka drink together and moan over their post-fight pains, to the ridicule and amusement of their respective wives. In an act of generosity, Mattis consoles Borka and tells him Borka's son Birk will be the next chief, as his own headstrong daughter has declared the robber way of life to be unethical: to steal from others does not match her worldview at all.<br><br>Borka's machismo enjoys a short, proud victory until Birk and Ronja stand up and swear in front of the entire robber community that they will never be robbers as long as they live.<br><br>Mattis just smiles sheepishly:<br><br>"Well, you know, Borka, children nowadays, they do what they want!"<br><br>Breaking patterns of hate, renouncing robbery, uniting two families, building bridges over deep pits, and daring to get to know the other side of the story: what a cheerful message after a dramatic adventure set in a fantasy version of a Swedish Medieval forest.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491581027i/22425285.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To the spirit of Ronja and Birk!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11945726119238529670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1678076617796439491"><b>Ronja rövardotter = Ronia, the Robber's Daughter, Astrid Lindgren </b><br/> <br/>Ronia, the Robber's Daughter is a children's fantasy book by the Swedish author Astrid Lindgren, first published in 1981. <br/><br/>Ronia is a girl growing up among a clan of robbers living in a castle in the woodlands of early-Medieval Scandinavia. As the only child of Matt, the chief, she is expected to become the leader of the clan someday. <br/><br/>Their castle, Matt's Fort, is split into two parts by a lightning bolt on the day of Ronia's birt</span>
  <span id="freeText1678076617796439491" style="display:none"><b>Ronja rövardotter = Ronia, the Robber's Daughter, Astrid Lindgren </b><br /> <br />Ronia, the Robber's Daughter is a children's fantasy book by the Swedish author Astrid Lindgren, first published in 1981. <br /><br />Ronia is a girl growing up among a clan of robbers living in a castle in the woodlands of early-Medieval Scandinavia. As the only child of Matt, the chief, she is expected to become the leader of the clan someday. <br /><br />Their castle, Matt's Fort, is split into two parts by a lightning bolt on the day of Ronia's birth. Ronia grows up with Matt's clan of robbers as her only company, until a rival robber group led by Borka moves into the other half of the castle, exacerbating the longstanding rivalry between the two bands. <br /><br />One day, Ronia sees Birk Borkason, the only son of Borka, idling by the chasm. He is the only other child she has ever met, and so she is sorry that he is a Borka. He engages her in a game of jumping across, which does not end until Birk almost falls down. Ronia saves him, and they eventually become friends. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز پانزدهم ماه آگوست سال 2005میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: رونیا،‌ دختر یک راهزن؛ نویسنده: آسترید لیندگرن؛ مترجم: نسرین وکیلی؛ تهران، چشمه، 1382؛ در 243ص، مصور، چاپ سوم 1389؛ شابک 9789643620660؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان سوئدی - سده 20م<br /><br />آغاز رخدادهای این داستان، در یک شب طوفانی است؛ در قلعه ی «مت راهزن»، و گروهش، به سبب زایش «رونیا»، دختر «مت»، شوری در آنجا برپاست؛ «رونیا» بزرگتر می‌شود، و رقصیدن، و فریاد برآوردن با راهزن‌ها را، می‌آموزد؛ اما تنها در جنگل است، که او احساس آرامش می‌کند؛ روزی «رونیا»، با «برک»، پسر دشمن بزرگ پدر خودش، آشنا می‌شود؛ زمانی از این آشنایی نمی‌گذرد، که کشمکش، میان دو گروه راهزن، دوباره درمی‌گیرد، و بدینسان، «رونیا» و «برک» نیز، در میانه ی همین کشمکش قرار می‌گیرند؛ و ....؛ <br /><br />نقل از متن: (و سپس صبح رسید؛ «رونیا» می‌خواست پیش «برک» برود؛ باید به سرعت می‌رفت؛ باید زمانی می‌رفت که هرکس دنبال کار صبحگاهی خود بود، و کسی در سرسرا نبود.؛ خیلی مراقب بود که کسی او را نبیند.؛ هر لحظه ممکن بود سر و کله‌ ی «نودل ـ پت» پیدا شود، و سئؤالی از او کند، و «رونیا» نمی‌خواست چنین فرصتی پیش آید.؛ با خود فکر کرد که در زیرزمین هم می‌تواند صبحانه‌ اش را بخورد.؛ به هر حال این‌جا راحت نمی‌شود چیز خورد.؛ پس با عجله مقداری نان در کیف چرمی خود چپاند، و شیر را در تنگ چوبی ریخت، و بدون این‌که کسی او را ببیند به طرف سردابه رفت.؛ خیلی زود به توده‌ ی سنگ‌ها رسید.؛ با این ترس که مبادا «برک» آن‌جا نباشد، صدا کرد: «برک»! از آن طرف سنگ‌ها کسی جواب نداد.؛ آن‌قدر مأیوس شد که می‌خواست گریه کند.؛ اگر نمی‌آمد چه؟ شاید به کل فراموش کرده بود.؛ از آن هم بدتر، شاید از قولی که داده بود پشیمان شده بود، به هر حال «رونیا» از نزدیکان «مت» بود، و دشمن «بورکا».؛ شاید اصلاً «برک» نمی‌خواست، با آدمی از این ایل و تبار رابطه داشته باشد.؛ ناگهان از پشت سر کسی موهای «رونیا» را کشید.؛ «رونیا» از ترس جیغ زد.؛ آیا این «نودل ـ پت» بود که دوباره مخفیانه آمده بود تا همه چیز را به هم بریزد؟ اما «نودل ـ پت» نبود.؛ «برک» بود.؛ همان‌جا ایستاده بود و می‌خندید، و سفیدی دندان‌هایش در تاریکی مشخص بود.؛ «رونیا» در روشنایی چراغی که در دست داشت، بیش از آن چیزی نمی‌دید.؛ «برک» گفت: خیلی وقت است منتظرت هستم.؛ «رونیا» گرمای شادی را درون خود احساس کرد.؛ فکرش را بکنید، برادری داشت که مدت زیادی به خاطر او انتظار کشیده بود! «رونیا» گفت: من هم همین‌طور.؛ از همان وقتی که از شر «رامفوب»‌ها خلاص شدم، منتظر بودم.؛ برای مدتی چیزی به فکرشان نرسید که درباره‌ اش صحبت کنند.؛ فقط همان‌جا ایستادند.؛ مات و مبهوت.؛ اما از این‌که دوباره با هم بودند، احساس خشنودی می‌کردند.»؛ پایان نقل<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 02/09/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12773880532052015836">Ronia was born on the night of the storm, when the fortress was cleft in halves by a lightning crack. Since that time the two robber clans – and bitter rivals - had lived either side of the divide. When Ronia was old enough to venture outside, after spending her growing years with her mother, father and the band of robbers, she was amazed to find the enchanted wood. She entertained herself daily until the day she saw the boy on the other side. Birk, also born on the night of the storm, was the s</span>
  <span id="freeText12773880532052015836" style="display:none">Ronia was born on the night of the storm, when the fortress was cleft in halves by a lightning crack. Since that time the two robber clans – and bitter rivals - had lived either side of the divide. When Ronia was old enough to venture outside, after spending her growing years with her mother, father and the band of robbers, she was amazed to find the enchanted wood. She entertained herself daily until the day she saw the boy on the other side. Birk, also born on the night of the storm, was the son of the Borka clan – Ronia was the daughter of Matt’s clan; but when the two children became friends, trouble struck. Sworn enemies should not be friends…<br /><br /><i>Ronia, the Robber’s Daughter</i> by Astrid Lindgren is a children’s book, designed for ages around 6 and up I would think. It was light, entertaining, filled with magic and mystery, and would be lots of fun for the appropriate age group. I read it for a challenge, borrowing it from my library. Recommended for children.<br /></span>

<div id="review_87486362" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87486362" />
    <a title="Meredith Holley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley"><img alt="Meredith Holley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548641865p2/1302775.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/87486362?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith Holley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith Holley" href="/user/show/1302775-meredith-holley">Meredith Holley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Madeleine L'Engle fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Meredith by: </span>
      Heather Svensson
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=best-of-the-year">best-of-the-year</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=up-hill-both-ways-in-the-snow">up-hill-both-ways-in-the-snow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=under-read-gems">under-read-gems</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=girls-rule">girls-rule</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1302775-meredith-holley?shelf=classic-young-reader">classic-young-reader</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer87486362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8278505852949888305">This was probably my favorite book I read in 2011. My friend gave it to me last year or the year before, and I always take a while to get to books that people have given me. I have to warm up to the concept of the book and get used to the cover and think about what mood would be the best for a read. I’m glad I waited so long to read it because the time/place for the read was perfect. I just enjoyed the hell out of this story. A lot of elements of the story hit my favorite things, and I loved its</span>
  <span id="freeText8278505852949888305" style="display:none">This was probably my favorite book I read in 2011. My friend gave it to me last year or the year before, and I always take a while to get to books that people have given me. I have to warm up to the concept of the book and get used to the cover and think about what mood would be the best for a read. I’m glad I waited so long to read it because the time/place for the read was perfect. I just enjoyed the hell out of this story. A lot of elements of the story hit my favorite things, and I loved its brightness and ease. <br /><br />Ronia is a wild harpy of a little girl who runs through the forest, tames wild horses, and lives in a cave when she has a fight with her father. Her mother sings the wolf song at bedtime and Ronia teaches herself not to be afraid. But, sometimes she still is afraid.<br /><br />I don’t have anything deep to say about this book, but for me it had just the right combination of reality and fantasy, sadness and hope. It didn’t shy away from harshness, but it wasn’t trying to beat me over the head with life. Maybe in another mood I would have been bothered by the fairy-tale quality of it, but I really loved that in this particular mood. It is also difficult to say how I would have felt about this as a kid, but I like to think I would have loved it. It has an unselfconscious wild girlness that I hope I’ve always loved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8278505852949888305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_49592513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49592513" />
    <a title="Manny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1713956-manny"><img alt="Manny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442491692p2/1713956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manny" href="/user/show/1713956-manny">Manny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1713956-manny?shelf=swedish-norwegian-and-danish">swedish-norwegian-and-danish</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49592513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4840042979930102081">There's this thing that happens to some children's authors who become too successful. They realise that every kid grows up reading their books, and they gradually start to feel that they ought to be, you know, telling them something <i>important</i> rather than just entertaining them...<br/><br/>So in this case we have Astrid Lindgren, who'd already written <i>Pippi Långstrump</i>, <i>Emil I Lönneberga</i>, <i>Karlsson På Taket</i> and several other timeless masterpieces. These books are as light as air, and any message they're impa</span>
  <span id="freeText4840042979930102081" style="display:none">There's this thing that happens to some children's authors who become too successful. They realise that every kid grows up reading their books, and they gradually start to feel that they ought to be, you know, telling them something <i>important</i> rather than just entertaining them...<br /><br />So in this case we have Astrid Lindgren, who'd already written <i>Pippi Långstrump</i>, <i>Emil I Lönneberga</i>, <i>Karlsson På Taket</i> and several other timeless masterpieces. These books are as light as air, and any message they're imparting sneaks in under your radar before you've even had a chance to figure out what it is. And now, here's Ronja, who's the daughter of a robber king that lives in a castle in the forest. On the night she's born, the castle is struck by lightning so that it splits down the middle. <br /><br />Her family discover, to their consternation, that a second band of robbers have moved into the other half of the divided castle. These people are their bitterest enemies. But Ronja falls in love with the son of the rival robber king, and, oh well, read it for yourself. You've probably figured out the main points already.<br /><br />If some lesser author had written this clunky piece of allegory, I suppose I might have thought it was more or less acceptable. But Astrid Lindgren?? I felt embarrassed from start to finish.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4840042979930102081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2112564837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8301659557480214726">I loved the book all the way through. The style really captured my fancy right away and found it beautifully written, authentic and heartfelt. I think it really captures the tug of the "tween" years, when children want to be more independent and begin to form their own ideas and wishes distinct from their parents, but also still yearn for that warmth and comfort and love and protection of being a child and having parents watch over you and assure you everything will be okay. And I appreciated th</span>
  <span id="freeText8301659557480214726" style="display:none">I loved the book all the way through. The style really captured my fancy right away and found it beautifully written, authentic and heartfelt. I think it really captures the tug of the "tween" years, when children want to be more independent and begin to form their own ideas and wishes distinct from their parents, but also still yearn for that warmth and comfort and love and protection of being a child and having parents watch over you and assure you everything will be okay. And I appreciated that we don't just see the child's perspective in this, but we see how it is a growing process for the parents, too. The parents are often voices of wisdom, though also the children sometimes have more wisdom than the parents and they all learn from one another! It is refreshing to see a book where the children learn that their parents aren't perfect, and that they should protect themselves from negative behaviors, but that even grown-ups can change for the better and still be lovable and needed. I adored the descriptions of nature and how the children were so connected to nature and the seasons and the animals. The children's spirits are free and it's beautiful. The few fantastical elements (harpies, dwarfs) wove seamlessly into the story. Wonderful!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8301659557480214726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10985113932940996414">When I had finished the previous book, a book translated from Swedish, J handed me this book, another book from Sweden. I was not familiar with the author until I saw she had written Pippi Longstocking - and of course I had heard of Pipi, even though I had never read any of her adventures.<br/><br/>I had a great time with this book. Not only was it translated literature, but also kid lit, which I adore. The author made you really love the world in which Ronia is growing up - you could practically hear the</span>
  <span id="freeText10985113932940996414" style="display:none">When I had finished the previous book, a book translated from Swedish, J handed me this book, another book from Sweden. I was not familiar with the author until I saw she had written Pippi Longstocking - and of course I had heard of Pipi, even though I had never read any of her adventures.<br /><br />I had a great time with this book. Not only was it translated literature, but also kid lit, which I adore. The author made you really love the world in which Ronia is growing up - you could practically hear the river, and smell the scents of the forest. Ronia is a wonderful character, full of life and exuberance, and her adventures in the forest just sparkle. Her budding relationship with Birk feels very real, I think because the author did not opt to make it simple. It's complicated, as is Ronia's relationship to her family.<br /><br />The characters in the book are not afraid to feel: the author gives them leave to gnash their teeth and throw things in anger, to wail and weep in sorrow, and leap and laugh with joy. And I think I liked that most of all.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1188959349268775708">This has been one of my favourite books ever since I first read it at around eight years of age. I hadn't re-read it in at least five years, though, and was amazed at all its subtleties: it deals gently, but without pretense, with themes of gender, politics, death, and above all growing up -- the bond between parents and children, the difficulties of letting go, and of becoming your own person. At the same time, it is a very enjoyable story of adventure and exploration; it has fantasy elements a</span>
  <span id="freeText1188959349268775708" style="display:none">This has been one of my favourite books ever since I first read it at around eight years of age. I hadn't re-read it in at least five years, though, and was amazed at all its subtleties: it deals gently, but without pretense, with themes of gender, politics, death, and above all growing up -- the bond between parents and children, the difficulties of letting go, and of becoming your own person. At the same time, it is a very enjoyable story of adventure and exploration; it has fantasy elements and a cast of likable, funny characters.<br /><br />Ronia ties with The Brothers Lionheart for my favourite Astrid Lindgren book. I believe both of them should be on every child's bookshelf, or better still, in the family library.<br /><br />(I should also mention the beautiful, evocative interior pen-and-ink illustrations by Ilon Wikland. They have become inseparable from the text for me. Utterly gorgeous, and they capture the atmosphere and emotional tenor of the books perfectly.)</span>

<div id="review_2449401215" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2449401215" />
    <a title="Lara Mi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21924792-lara-mi"><img alt="Lara Mi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548829956p2/21924792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2449401215?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lara Mi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lara Mi" href="/user/show/21924792-lara-mi">Lara Mi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780192789945" href="/book/show/10595727-ronia-the-robber-s-daughter">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=5-friendship">5-friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=2-english-translated">2-english-translated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=6-thieves-pirates-and-assassins">6-thieves-pirates-and-assassins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=1-fantasy">1-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=novel-owned">novel-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=2-movie-adaptation">2-movie-adaptation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=5-romantic-sub-plot">5-romantic-sub-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=5-old-houses-and-castles-to-explore">5-old-houses-and-castles-to-explore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21924792-lara-mi?shelf=5-forests">5-forests</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2449401215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5411142271452462119"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478991849i/21137618.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>"How good it was to love someone so much that there was no need to fear even the most difficult thing."</blockquote><br/>Deep in an enchanted forest lives Ronia in her father's fortress - chieftain of Matt's robbers. Much loved by her parents and robbers alike, she grows up being doted upon and loving the wild enchanted forest around her. But then Ronia meets Birk - the son of her father's worst enemy. The two form a close friendship which must be kept a secret if they are to keep seeing each other.<br/><br/><b>Ronia, The R</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5411142271452462119" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478991849i/21137618.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>"How good it was to love someone so much that there was no need to fear even the most difficult thing."</blockquote><br>Deep in an enchanted forest lives Ronia in her father's fortress - chieftain of Matt's robbers. Much loved by her parents and robbers alike, she grows up being doted upon and loving the wild enchanted forest around her. But then Ronia meets Birk - the son of her father's worst enemy. The two form a close friendship which must be kept a secret if they are to keep seeing each other.<br><br><b>Ronia, The Robber's Daughter</b> is one of the few stories I would consider perfect in its entirety. Growing up, I used to watch the 1984's live-action movie which I always enjoyed. It was never a major favourite of mine, but one I always held fond memories of. When it came to actually reading the book, I was a bit hesitant; I didn't enjoy author Astrid Lindgren's other book <b>Pippi Longstocking</b> at all - would I be able to enjoy other works by her or would I ruin nice memories of the film?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532330224i/26015425.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Luckily, <b>Ronia, The Robber's Daughter</b> was nothing like the other book. The writing - the English translation in any case - was just to my liking, a third-person narrative that gave the right amount of what Ronia thinks and feels while also keeping a neutral point of view on the other characters. The descriptions of the woods and fortress are beautifully written and most importantly, the characters had such depth and such heartfelt emotions. <br><br>The ties between Ronia and her parents, especially her father Matt, are shown in such a loving way - I can't think of a dearer father-daughter relationship in any other story I've come across before. And though robbers they are, all the members of Matt's band of robbers are quite loveable in a way, just as they all love Ronia. It is all the more difficult when Ronia learns to love Birk and finds herself torn between him and the love for her father. <br><br>Ronia and Birk's relationship is just the sweetest. Young as they are, they form a very strong bond and call each other brother and sister. They go to great lengths to support each other and although they frequently argue, there doesn't seem to be a thing that can keep the two apart. I also love how this book leaves room for interpretation; they are young and can most certainly simply be friends or like brother and sister - yet if you prefer, well you can just go by a quote of Birk's mother:<br><blockquote>"Oh, yes, we all know what that will mean in a year or two!"</blockquote><br>The forest has just a touch of magic that you think there might just be a real one like that somewhere out there. Yet I find the magical creatures shown in this book quite unique - there are dwarves and harpies, but they seem different from ones we see in other stories. The time Ronia spends out in the forest is both adventurous as just absolutely lovely to picture with the changing of the days and seasons. <br><br>The struggles and joys the characters face are also written in such a believable manner, one can't help but feel with them. Just as much as Ronia's and Birk's attempt to ignore the dangers around them just to enjoy another day in each other's company. It's just such a lovely book about bonds between people, the willingness to give and do for others, and all that in the midst of an enchanted forest. To put a cherry on top, <b>Ghibli</b> has made a TV series based on this book which I am super excited to begin watching - this book plus <b>Ghibli</b> can't be anything short of amazing!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1532331247i/26015484.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5411142271452462119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1840327103" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9782013220538" href="/book/show/995211.Ronya_fille_de_brigand">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15972406-zaz?shelf=0-250p">0-250p</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15972406-zaz?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15972406-zaz?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15972406-zaz?shelf=children-books">children-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1840327103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6375025479963553744">Rererereread (etc). A good book about an independent and strong headed little girl, reading to break the rules to have fun with her friend.<br/><br/>Ronya (I'll use the French spelling for the names) is the daughter of Mattis, a brigand. She lives in his castle with all the robbers and spends her time in the woods. On day, Ronya meets Rik, the son of Matthis' sworn enemy and of course nobody approves this new friendship.<br/><br/>As usual, the story was pleasant, plunging the young reader in a period when brigands </span>
  <span id="freeText6375025479963553744" style="display:none">Rererereread (etc). A good book about an independent and strong headed little girl, reading to break the rules to have fun with her friend.<br /><br />Ronya (I'll use the French spelling for the names) is the daughter of Mattis, a brigand. She lives in his castle with all the robbers and spends her time in the woods. On day, Ronya meets Rik, the son of Matthis' sworn enemy and of course nobody approves this new friendship.<br /><br />As usual, the story was pleasant, plunging the young reader in a period when brigands existed, people lived in castles and when having fun was summarized by robbing people, eating, singing and wandering in the woods. It was nice to follow Ronya's life in the woods, it was simple but well developed, and the additions of fantastical creatures (evil elves, dwarves, etc) gave a nice frightening tone to some events. On the characters' side, Ronya was a nice, strong headed and independent little girl, making her very likable, and I enjoyed how balanced her relationship with Rik was. Mattis was overacting all the time, which was funny to see, especially for a chief, and it was interesting that Ronya was entitled to her own opinions regarding how he treated Rik, herself, or the poor robbed people. Because of the lack of true time period and Lingdren's witty writing, the story aged really well and I found it as pleasant as when I was a kid.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6375025479963553744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1430933423" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1430933423" />
    <a title="E.F.B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39244832-e-f-b"><img alt="E.F.B." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424876183p2/39244832.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1430933423?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="E.F.B." class="user" itemprop="url" name="E.F.B." href="/user/show/39244832-e-f-b">E.F.B.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Children ages 8-12</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to E.F.B. by: </span>
      TORn Book Club
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=torn-bookclub-books">torn-bookclub-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1430933423" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11426208010827997804">From the description on the back of my copy of the book: “On the night Ronia was born, a thunderstorm raged over the mountain, but in Matt’s castle and among his band of robbers there was only joy—for Matt now had a spirited little black-haired daughter. Soon Ronia learns to dance and yell with the robbers, but it is alone in the forest that she feels truly at home. Then one day Ronia meets Birk, the son of Matt’s arch-enemy. Soon after Ronia and Birk become friends, the worst quarrel ever betwe</span>
  <span id="freeText11426208010827997804" style="display:none">From the description on the back of my copy of the book: “On the night Ronia was born, a thunderstorm raged over the mountain, but in Matt’s castle and among his band of robbers there was only joy—for Matt now had a spirited little black-haired daughter. Soon Ronia learns to dance and yell with the robbers, but it is alone in the forest that she feels truly at home. Then one day Ronia meets Birk, the son of Matt’s arch-enemy. Soon after Ronia and Birk become friends, the worst quarrel ever between the rival bands erupts, and Ronia and Birk are right in the middle.” <br /><br />My review: I first heard of “Ronia, the Robber’s Daughter” when it was assigned as the book of the month for TORn Bookclub. I had never read anything by Astrid Lindgren before, so I didn’t know what to expect, but I decided to give it a go because it looked interesting. I was pleasantly surprised. Ronia is a quirky, fun, and brave young girl and her antics were very entertaining. At the same time, her friendship with Birk was strong and sweet, which I liked a lot, and though it did cause a strain between them and their families at first, it ultimately brought everyone closer together. <br /><br />For those wondering if this book would be a good read for their child, I would say children from ages 8-12 would probably enjoy it the most. It might be okay for younger children if they were having it read to them, but it should be noted that there is some violence and the threat of violence between the rival robber bands here and there throughout the story, though nothing is ever described graphically. Also, Ronia and Birk find themselves in peril several times, usually because of the mythical creatures that live in the forest. The harpies in particular are the most threatening, and really, really, young children might find them scary. But really, I think if your child enjoys things like “The Hobbit”, for example, they’ll enjoy “Ronia, the Robber’s Daughter” as well. They very much have a similar, light-hearted, fairytale feel, though “Ronia” doesn’t do anywhere near as much traveling as “The Hobbit”, nor are there any epic battles.<br /><br />My only personal complaint about this book is that the pacing was a little slow in places, especially at the beginning, but it is intended for young children, so I expected that. Over all, I give it a solid four out of five stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11426208010827997804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_180537525" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180537525" />
    <a title="Alexis Neal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3781253-alexis-neal"><img alt="Alexis Neal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277155282p2/3781253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180537525?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexis Neal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexis Neal" href="/user/show/3781253-alexis-neal">Alexis Neal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3781253-alexis-neal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3781253-alexis-neal?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3781253-alexis-neal?shelf=breakfast-club">breakfast-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180537525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8489419305933512240">Another classic from my childhood. Lindgren is a very capable Swedish author (best known for <i>Pippi Longstocking</i> and <i>Mio, My Son</i>), and this book is a great example. Lindgren presents the life of a robber's daughter quite compellingly--the day to day pleasures of life in and around the woods are told in vivid detail; the reality of robbing and other adult concerns are only vaguely addressed. In that sense, it is very like a child's view of life. Ronia, the title character, is spunky and courageous</span>
  <span id="freeText8489419305933512240" style="display:none">Another classic from my childhood. Lindgren is a very capable Swedish author (best known for <i>Pippi Longstocking</i> and <i>Mio, My Son</i>), and this book is a great example. Lindgren presents the life of a robber's daughter quite compellingly--the day to day pleasures of life in and around the woods are told in vivid detail; the reality of robbing and other adult concerns are only vaguely addressed. In that sense, it is very like a child's view of life. Ronia, the title character, is spunky and courageous, and her friendship with Birk, the rival chieftain's son, is quite touching. The family unit is portrayed fairly well. There is some violence, though it's mostly fear of things <i>about</i> to happen--there is not much gore. Overall, the book has good things to say about the foolishness of feuds (and possibly even racism), the wisdom of children, the love of a father for his daughter, the importance of friendship, and the morality of robbery as a career. The story largely reads like a children's story--that is, a story from the child's point of view. Some problems loom larger, while others recede into almost nothing...and not the problems you'd expect from an adult point of view. It's artfully done, and the result is a fun yet compelling story. Which is hardly surprising, from Lindgren.<br /><br />Definitely worth reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8489419305933512240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12744624774971285135" style="display:none">Best book ever! Oh, and the picture on the cover...Ronia is so hot! She's how I imagined myself to be in my ten-year-old dreams. <br /><br />On a dark and stormy night, a huge bolt of lightning shot down from the sky and SPLIT Matt's Fort in two. That was the night that robber Matt's daughter, Ronia, was born. But that same night, another baby was born...Birk, son of Matt's robber rival, Borka. They are the only two children in the forest...are they to be friends, or enemies? <br /><br />What follows are the adventures of of wild and free children who have the run of their entire world, who take risks and know how to live in the forest, even though it's full of harpies, rumptrolls, and bears who would do them harm. Noora my Finland friend later on also recommended this book, so I assumed it must be a classic for children in Europe.<br/><br/>I am not disappointed. I love all the characters: the no-nonsense of Lovis, the childlike qualities of Matt and all the other robbers. Every aspect of the book is pretty much just-right. It is light and funny but also has serious parts. Very well-balanced, I should say. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MEGIVStAz0t3icwQu/vYNcerWFpDx6otuFpVrgRwaRMKZ+GHkB4GI9CieHFMDtLqEfS/ko1KJErjJBMfyTObiQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eTmaV9oeKh8wc19/YsHG4wSuaYLmBfgIAb+3RghKSEFDH/OFYUDjd5dY6x6VNMw80vGOSiiIdm9awfH3xQm62w==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11270148250334683172">Astrid Anna Emilia Lindgren, née Ericsson, (1907 - 2002) was a Swedish children's book author and screenwriter, whose many titles were translated into 85 languages and published in more than 100 countries. She has sold roughly 165 million copies worldwide. Today, she is most remembered for writing the <i>Pippi Longstocking</i> books, as well as the <i>Karlsson-on-the-Roof</i> book series.<br/><br/>Awards:<br/>Hans Christian A</span>
  <span id="freeText11270148250334683172" style="display:none">Astrid Anna Emilia Lindgren, née Ericsson, (1907 - 2002) was a Swedish children's book author and screenwriter, whose many titles were translated into 85 languages and published in more than 100 countries. She has sold roughly 165 million copies worldwide. Today, she is most remembered for writing the <i>Pippi Longstocking</i> books, as well as the <i>Karlsson-on-the-Roof</i> book series.<br /><br />Awards:<br />Hans Christian Andersen Award for Writing (1958)</span>
